
# Information Extraction with nltk


```python
import nltk, re, pprint
```

The ease or difficulty with which information may be extracted from text depend largely on it's nature, with information extraction being significantly easier in structured text in contrast to unstructured ones which remain a challenge for natural language processing.

** *Structured Texts* **
These include texts in Structured databases, tables and those restricted to very specific domains in which the structure of speech is highly uniform.
- Tables

>>>>>| Organistion | Location |
| ----------- | -------- |
| Omnicom     | New York |
| DDB Needham | New York |
| Kaplan Thaler Group| New York|
| BBDO South  | Atlanta  |
| Georgia-Pacific| Atlanta|

We may extract information about location from the above text with the algorithm below

1 Convert tables into a list of tuples


```python
locs = [
    ('Omnicom', 'IN', 'New York'),
    ('DDB Needham', 'IN', 'New York'),
    ('Kaplan Thaler Group', 'IN', 'New York'),
    ('BBDO South', 'IN', 'Atlanta'),
    ('Georgia-pacific', 'IN', 'Atlanta'),
]
locs[1]
```




    ('DDB Needham', 'IN', 'New York')




```python
def ret_loc(loc):
    query_loc = [e1 for (e1,e2,e3) in locs if e3 == loc]
    if len(query_loc) != 0:
        print(query_loc)
    else:
        print("No result matches request")
```


```python
ret_loc('Atlanta')
```

    ['BBDO South', 'Georgia-pacific']
    


```python
def ret_org(org):
    query_org = [e3 for (e1,e2,e3) in locs if e1 == org]
    if len(query_org) != 0:
        print(query_org)
    else:
        print("No result matches request")
```


```python
ret_org('New York')
```

    No result matches request
    


```python
def ie_preprocess(document):
    sentences = nltk.sent_tokenize(document)
    sentences = [nltk.word_tokenize(sent) for sent in sentences]
    pos = [nltk.pos_tag(word) for word in sentences]
    return pos
```


```python
ie_preprocess("I am a boy")
```




    [[('I', 'PRP'), ('am', 'VBP'), ('a', 'DT'), ('boy', 'NN')]]




```python
k = nltk.word_tokenize("I am a boy")
```


```python
nltk.pos_tag(k)
```




    [('I', 'PRP'), ('am', 'VBP'), ('a', 'DT'), ('boy', 'NN')]



## Chunking


```python
doc = """As we can see, NP-chunks are often smaller pieces than complete noun phrases. For example, the market for
system-management software for Digital's hardware is a single noun phrase (containing two nested noun
phrases), but it is captured in NP-chunks by the simpler chunk the market. One of the motivations for this
difference is that NP-chunks are defined so as not to contain other NP-chunks. Consequently, any prepositional
phrases or subordinate clauses that modify a nominal will not be included in the corresponding NP-chunk,
since they almost certainly contain further noun phrases."""

grammar = r"""NP: {<DT>?<NN|NNP|NNS|NNPS><IN><DT>?<JJ>*<NN|NNP|NNS><IN>?<NN|NNP|NNS|JJ>?<NN|NNP|NNS>?<POS>?<NN|NNP|NNS>?}
                  {<DT|PP$>?<JJ>*<NN|NNP|NNS>}
                  {<NN|NNP|NNS|NNPS>+}
           """
d = ie_preprocess(doc)
cp = nltk.RegexpParser(grammar)
result = cp.parse(d[3])
pprint.pprint(result)
```

    Tree('S', [('Consequently', 'RB'), (',', ','), Tree('NP', [('any', 'DT'), ('prepositional', 'JJ'), ('phrases', 'NNS')]), ('or', 'CC'), Tree('NP', [('subordinate', 'JJ'), ('clauses', 'NNS')]), ('that', 'WDT'), ('modify', 'VBP'), ('a', 'DT'), ('nominal', 'JJ'), ('will', 'MD'), ('not', 'RB'), ('be', 'VB'), ('included', 'VBN'), ('in', 'IN'), Tree('NP', [('the', 'DT'), ('corresponding', 'JJ'), ('NP-chunk', 'NNP')]), (',', ','), ('since', 'IN'), ('they', 'PRP'), ('almost', 'RB'), ('certainly', 'RB'), ('contain', 'VBP'), Tree('NP', [('further', 'JJ'), ('noun', 'NN')]), Tree('NP', [('phrases', 'NNS')]), ('.', '.')])
    


```python
from nltk.corpus import brown

chunk = r"""CHUNK: {<V.*><TO><V.*>}
{<DT>?<NN|NNP|NNS|NNPS><IN><DT>?<JJ>*<NN|NNP|NNS><IN>?<NN|NNP|NNS|JJ>?<NN|NNP|NNS>?<POS>?<NN|NNP|NNS>?}"""
cc = nltk.RegexpParser(chunk)


for sent in brown.tagged_sents():
    tree = cc.parse(sent)
    for subtree in tree.subtrees():
        if subtree.label() == "CHUNK":
            print(subtree)
```

```python
#converting IOB chunk tags to trees

text = """
he PRP BNP
accepted VBD BVP
the DT BNP
position NN INP
of IN BPP
vice NN BNP
chairman NN INP
of IN BPP
Carlyle NNP BNP
Group NNP INP
, , O
a DT BNP
merchant NN INP
banking NN INP
concern NN INP 
. . O
"""

nltk.chunk.conllstr2tree(text, chunk_types=['NP']).draw()
```

### Increasing chunking accuracy 

#### N-Gram Chunkers


```python
class UnigramChunker(nltk.ChunkParserI):
    def __init__(self, train_sent):
        self.train_tagger = [[(t,c) for w,t,c in nltk.tree2conlltags(sent)] for sent in train_sent]
        self.tagger = nltk.UnigramTagger(self.train_tagger)
    
    def parse(self, sentence):
        pos_tags = [pos for (word, pos) in sentence]
        tagged_pos_tag = self.tagger.tag(pos_tags)
        chunktags = [chunktag for (pos, chunktag) in tagged_pos_tag]
        conlltags = [(word, pos, chunktag) for ((word,pos), chunktag) in zip(sentence, chunktags)]
        return nltk.chunk.conlltags2tree(conlltags)
```


```python
test_sent = conll2000.chunked_sents('test.txt', chunk_types=['NP'])
train_sent = conll2000.chunked_sents('train.txt', chunk_types=['NP'])

unigramchunker = UnigramChunker(train_sent)
#unigramchunker.parse(ie_preprocess(doc)[1]).draw()
print(unigramchunker.evaluate(test_sent))
```

    ChunkParse score:
        IOB Accuracy:  92.9%
        Precision:     79.9%
        Recall:        86.8%
        F-Measure:     83.2%

```python
class BigramChunker(nltk.ChunkParserI):
    def __init__(self, train_sent):
        self.train_tagger = [[(t,c) for w,t,c in nltk.tree2conlltags(sent)] for sent in train_sent]
        self.tagger = nltk.BigramTagger(self.train_tagger)
    
    def parse(self, sentence):
        pos_tags = [pos for (word, pos) in sentence]
        tagged_pos_tag = self.tagger.tag(pos_tags)
        chunktags = [chunktag for (pos, chunktag) in tagged_pos_tag]
        conlltags = [(word, pos, chunktag) for ((word,pos), chunktag) in zip(sentence, chunktags)]
        return nltk.chunk.conlltags2tree(conlltags)
```


```python
bigramchunker = BigramChunker(train_sent)
bigramchunker.parse(ie_preprocess(doc)[1]).draw()
print(bigramchunker.evaluate(test_sent))
```

    ChunkParse score:
        IOB Accuracy:  93.3%
        Precision:     82.3%
        Recall:        86.8%
        F-Measure:     84.5%
    


```python
class TrigramChunker(nltk.ChunkParserI):
    def __init__(self, train_sent):
        self.train_tagger = [[(t,c) for w,t,c in nltk.tree2conlltags(sent)] for sent in train_sent]
        self.tagger = nltk.TrigramTagger(self.train_tagger)
    
    def parse(self, sentence):
        pos_tags = [pos for (word, pos) in sentence]
        tagged_pos_tag = self.tagger.tag(pos_tags)
        chunktags = [chunktag for (pos, chunktag) in tagged_pos_tag]
        conlltags = [(word, pos, chunktag) for ((word,pos), chunktag) in zip(sentence, chunktags)]
        #print("{}\n{}\n{}".format(pos_tags, chunktags,conlltags))
        return nltk.chunk.conlltags2tree(conlltags)
```


```python
trigramchunker = TrigramChunker(train_sent)
trigramchunker.parse(ie_preprocess(doc)[1]).draw()
print(trigramchunker.evaluate(test_sent))
```

    ChunkParse score:
        IOB Accuracy:  93.3%
        Precision:     82.5%
        Recall:        86.8%
        F-Measure:     84.6%
    

#### Maximum entropy chunker


```python
class ConsecutiveNPChunkParser(nltk.TaggerI):
    def __init__(self, train_sents):
        self.train_set = []
        for tagged_sent in train_sents:
            untagged_sent = nltk.tag.untag(tagged_sent)
            history = []
            for i, (word, tag) in enumerate(tagged_sent):
                feature_sets = npchunk_features(untagged_sent, i, history)
                self.train_set.append((feature_sets, tag))
                history.append(tag)
        self.classifier = nltk.MaxentClassifier.train(self.train_set, algorithm='megam', trace=0)
        
        def tag(self, ssentence):
            history = []
            for i, word in enumerate(sentence):
                feature_sets = npchunk_features(sentence, i, history)
                tag = self.classifier.classify(feature_sets)
                history.append(tag)
            return zip(sentence, history)
```


```python
class ConsecutiveNPChunker(nltk.ChunkParserI):
    def __init__(self, train_sents):
        tagged_sents = [[((w,t), c) for (w,t,c) in nltk.chunk.tree2conlltags(sent)] for sent in train_sents]
        self.tagger =  ConsecutiveNPChunkParser(tagged_sents)
        
    def parse(self, sentence):
        tagged_sents = self.tagger.tag(sentence)
        conlltags = [(w,t,c) for ((w,t), c) in tagged_sents]
        return nltk.chunk.conlltags2tree(conlltags)
```


```python
def npchunk_features(sentence, i, history):
    word, pos = sentence[i]
    if i == 0:
        prev_word, prev_pos = "<START>", "<START>"
    else:
        prevword, prev_pos = sentence[i-1]
    return {"pos": pos, "prev_pos": prev_pos}
```


```python
chunker = ConsecutiveNPChunker(train_sent)
print(chunker.evaluate(test_sent))
```


```python
sent = [("Oni","DT"),("omo","NN"),("e","VB"),("ole","PRP"),("ma","NEG"),("kiaze","VB"),("emi","NN"),("ni","WP"),("u","PRP"),("a","VB"),("lu","VB"), ("ekeli","IN"), ("aze","NN"), ("na", "DT")]
grammar = r"""
PP: {<IN><NP>}
NP: {<NN.*>+}
NP: {<PRP>}
NP: {<DT><NN.*>}
NP: {<NP><DT>}
NP: {<NP><PP>}
CLAUSE: {<NP><VP>}
CLAUSE: {<DT>?<NP><VP><NP>*<PP>*}
C-CLAUSE: {<WP><NN.*|PRP|NP><VP>+}
VP: {<VB.*>+}
VP: {<VB.*><NP|PP|CLAUSE>+$}
"""

cp = nltk.RegexpParser(grammar, loop=3)
#print(cp.parse(sent))
cp.parse(sent).draw()
```

    (S
      Oni/DT
      (CLAUSE (NP omo/NN) (VP e/VB))
      (NP ole/PRP)
      ma/NEG
      (VP kiaze/VB)
      (NP emi/NN)
      ni/WP
      (CLAUSE (NP u/PRP) (VP a/VB lu/VB))
      (PP ekeli/IN (NP (NP aze/NN) na/DT)))
    


```python
NP1 = nltk.Tree('NP', ['Jesse'])
NP2 = nltk.Tree('NP', ['the', 'rabbit'])
VP = nltk.Tree('VP', ['love', NP2])
T0 = nltk.Tree('T\'', ['does', VP])
TP = nltk.Tree('TP', [NP1, T0])
print(TP)
print(TP[1][1].label())
TP.draw()
```

    (TP (NP Jesse) (T' does (VP love (NP the rabbit))))
    VP
